href="mailto:?subject=NYTimes.com%3A%20What%20We%20Know%20and%20Don%E2%80%99t%20About%20the%20Trump-Ukraine%20Affair&amp;body=From%20The%20New%20York%20Times%3A%0A%0AWhat%20We%20Know%20and%20Don%E2%80%99t%20About%20the%20Trump-Ukraine%20Affair%0A%0AThe%20major%20question%20is%20whether%20President%20Trump%20used%20American%20foreign%20policy%20to%20try%20to%20damage%20a%20political%20rival.%0A%0Ahttps%3A%2F%2Fwww.nytimes.com%2F2019%2F09%2F25%2Fus%2Fpolitics%2Fukraine-trump-whistleblower.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><svg class="css-4brsb6" height="9" viewbox="0 0 15 9" width="15"><path clip-rule="evenodd" d="M.906 8.418V0L5.64 4.76.906 8.419zm13 0L9.174 4.761 13.906 0v8.418zM7.407 6.539l-1.13-1.137L.907 9h13l-5.37-3.598-1.13 1.137zM1.297 0h12.22l-6.11 5.095L1.297 0z" fill="#000" fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></a></li><li class="css-60hakz"><div class="css-6n7j50"><button aria-expanded="false" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="More sharing options" class="css-16ogagc" data-testid=""><svg class="css-uhuo44" height="13" viewbox="0 0 16 13" width="16"><path clip-rule="evenodd" d="M15.406 5.359L8.978 0v3.215C3.82 3.215.406 8.107.406 12.66 1.653 9.133 4.29 7.517 8.978 7.517v3.2l6.428-5.358z" fill="#000" fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></button></div></li><li class="css-60hakz"></li><li class="css-l72opv"></li></ul></div></div></li></ul></div></header></div><section class="meteredContent css-1i2y565" itemprop="articleBody" name="articleBody"><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">WASHINGTON — Speaker Nancy Pelosi announced <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/24/us/politics/democrats-impeachment-trump.html?module=inline" title="">a formal impeachment inquiry</a> on Tuesday amid mounting furor over <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/us/politics/ukraine-transcript-trump.html?module=inline" title="">President Trump’s</a> efforts to pressure Ukraine’s government to investigate former <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/us/politics/ukraine-transcript-trump.html?module=inline" title="">Vice President Joseph R. Biden Jr.,</a> apparently the subject of a classified whistle-blower complaint the administration refused for weeks to show to Congress before <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/24/us/politics/trump-whistleblower-congress.html?module=inline" title="">dropping</a> objections. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Trump, meanwhile, said he planned on Wednesday to release the transcript of a phone call he had in July with <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/world/europe/ukraine-trump-whistleblower-zelensky.html?module=inline" title="">President Volodymyr Zelensky of Ukraine</a>. Mr. Trump insisted it would show that he said nothing inappropriate, but scrutiny about his conduct toward Ukraine has <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/23/us/politics/trump-un-biden-ukraine.html?module=inline" title="">spread beyond</a> the single conversation.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Here are some of the basic facts behind the controversy.</p><h2 class="css-ani50b eoo0vm40" id="link-31a9d924">What did Mr. Trump do?</h2><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0"><a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/us/politics/ukraine-transcript-trump.html?module=inline" title="">Mr. Trump</a> is said to have pressured <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/us/politics/ukraine-transcript-trump.html?module=inline" title="">Mr. Zelensky</a> to investigate Mr. Biden and his younger son, Hunter — both directly and through a proxy, Rudolph W. Giuliani, one of Mr. Trump’s personal lawyers. As a leading candidate to be the Democratic Party’s 2020 presidential nominee, Mr. Biden is Mr. Trump’s political rival.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">As vice president, Mr. Biden <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.cfr.org/event/foreign-affairs-issue-launch-former-vice-president-joe-biden" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">pushed the Ukrainian government in 2015 to fire its top prosecutor, Viktor Shokin</a>, who was widely seen as an obstacle to reform because he failed to bring corruption cases. At the time, Mr. Biden’s son sat on the board of a Ukrainian energy company, Burisma Holdings. </p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Trump and his allies have insinuated, without evidence, that Mr. Biden was trying to protect the company from prosecution. An investigation into him, even if it were unfounded or turned up no evidence of a crime, could damage his campaign prospects by suggesting wrongdoing.</p><h2 class="css-ani50b eoo0vm40" id="link-3e296523">Did Mr. Trump use American foreign policy to try to damage a political rival?</h2><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">This is the big question. The White House froze more than $391 million in military assistance to <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/us/politics/ukraine-phone-call-transcript.html?module=inline" title="">Ukraine</a> this summer that Congress had appropriated. The money was intended to help Ukraine defend itself from Russian territorial aggression, including a military conflict in eastern Ukraine that has killed more than 13,000 people since 2014. </p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><figure aria-label="media" class="sizeMedium css-qhlm6o" itemprop="associatedMedia" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/VideoObject" role="group"><meta content="2019-09-25T21:44:31.000Z" itemprop="uploadDate"/><meta content="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/23/world/23zelensky1/merlin_159599388_1f8d9b23-32a8-4978-833a-1f95eaa82701-articleLarge.jpg" itemprop="thumbnailUrl"/><meta content="President Trump is facing calls for impeachment related to a phone call with Ukrainian president Volodymyr Zelensky. A reconstructed transcript of the call appears to show the president asking Zelensky to investigate a political rival, Joe Biden, and his son Hunter. Zelensky denied this. “I think, and you read it, that nobody pushed, pushed me, yes.” “In other words, no pressure.” Here’s a closer look at Ukraine’s leader. He’s a first-time politician who won a landslide victory in May with more than 73 percent of the vote. He beat Petro Poroshenko, who he argued did little to combat rampant corruption. Before entering politics, Zelensky was a comedian and the star of a popular TV series. In a case of life imitating art, Zelensky played a teacher who unexpectedly became president after a speech on anti-corruption went viral. His major priority is ending the war with Russia. Zelensky uses social media to push his image as an everyman, posting selfies, showing off his vacation in the Black Sea, enjoying Ukraine’s sunflower fields and working out. Zelensky is now in a tough spot. He’s caught between wanting to build good relations with the U.S. and getting stuck in the middle of an American political scandal. “I’m sorry, but I don’t want to be involved to, democratic, open — elections. Elections of U.S.A.”" itemprop="transcript"/><div class="css-bsn42l"><span class="css-1dv1kvn">Video</span><div><div class="css-1t0v8sy etkm6pg0"><div class="css-mm3pwi"></div><div class="css-1a74oa6 etkm6pg1"><div class="css-1ihorw etkm6pg2"><img alt="Video player loading" src="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/23/world/23zelensky1/23zelensky1-videoSixteenByNine3000.jpg"/></div><div class="css-1ruigs3"><div class="css-v15h5m"><div></div><div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><figcaption class="css-17ai7jg emkp2hg0" itemprop="caption description name"><span class="css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0">President Trump is facing calls for impeachment related to a phone call with Ukraine’s president. Who’s the man on the other end of the phone?</span><span class="css-cch8ym"><span class="css-1dv1kvn">Credit</span><span class="emkp2hg2 css-1nwzsjy e1z0qqy90" itemprop="copyrightHolder"><span class="css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0">Credit</span><span>Sergey Dolzhenko/EPA, via Shutterstock</span></span></span></figcaption></figure><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0"><a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/us/politics/ukraine-phone-call-transcript.html?module=inline" title="">Mr. Trump</a> has given conflicting explanations for the freeze. On Monday, he cited corruption in Ukraine as the reason for the delay. On Tuesday, he instead said he had held up the military assistance because European countries had not paid their fair share to help defend Ukraine, a former Soviet republic, from Russian incursions.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Trump directed Mick Mulvaney, the acting White House chief of staff, <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/23/us/politics/trump-un-biden-ukraine.html?module=inline" title="">to pause the aid</a> in the days before his July phone call with <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/us/politics/ukraine-phone-call-transcript.html?module=inline" title="">Mr. Zelensky</a>, senior administration officials said. The Trump administration abruptly <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/12/us/politics/ukraine-aid-white-house.html?module=inline" title="">unfroze the package</a> this month amid mounting questions about what Mr. Trump was doing with Ukraine.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><h2 class="css-ani50b eoo0vm40" id="link-508d1b81">Why is this coming up now?</h2><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">An intelligence official <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/19/us/politics/intelligence-whistle-blower-complaint-trump.html?action=click&amp;module=inline&amp;pgtype=Article&amp;region=Footer" title="">filed a whistle-blower complaint last month</a> about the president’s actions. The inspector general for the intelligence community deemed the complaint “credible” and “urgent” and forwarded it to the acting director of national intelligence, Joseph Maguire, under a law <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/20/us/whistleblower-law-explained.html?module=inline" title="">that says</a> such complaints must be shown to Congress within a week. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">But Mr. Maguire refused to share the complaint with Congress, saying the Justice Department disagreed with the inspector general’s conclusion that its subject matter was covered under the law that requires disclosing such complaints to Congress. The issue came into the open when the House Intelligence Committee chairman, Representative Adam B. Schiff, Democrat of California, sent an <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/17/us/politics/dni-whistleblower-complaint.html?module=inline" title="">angry letter to Mr. Maguire on Sept. 10</a>, accusing him of <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/20/us/whistleblower-law-explained.html?module=inline" title="">violating the law.</a> </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Maguire <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/24/us/politics/trump-whistleblower-congress.html?module=inline" title="">relented</a> as the <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/09/25/us/politics/trump-ukraine-transcript.html?module=inline" title="">impeachment inquiry</a> came into focus. He was expected to release a redacted version of the complaint in coming days, people familiar with the situation said late on Tuesday. Administration officials were also said to be working on a deal to allow the whistle-blower to file the complaint to congressional investigators. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Maguire is set to testify about the matter on Thursday.</p><h2 class="css-ani50b eoo0vm40" id="link-6e675228">What did the whistle-blower claim?</h2><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The complaint’s full details remain a mystery, as does the <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/09/25/us/politics/trump-ukraine-transcript.html?module=inline" title="">whistle-blower’s</a> identity. Because Mr. Trump and Mr. Giuliani have openly acknowledged pressuring Ukraine about “corruption” and the Bidens, it is not clear how much the complaint involves that is not already in plain view. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">But in a closed-door briefing with the House Intelligence Committee, the inspector general for the intelligence community, Michael Atkinson, <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/19/us/politics/intelligence-whistle-blower-complaint-trump.html?module=inline" title="">said that the complaint involved multiple actions, according to two officials familiar with his briefing</a>, suggesting that the matter goes beyond Mr. Trump’s July phone call.</p><h2 class="css-ani50b eoo0vm40" id="link-1de80b6">What does Mr. Trump say?</h2><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The president insists that he has been unfairly accused, saying — without offering evidence — that the whistle-blower is “partisan” and that Democrats and the news media are initiating a new “witch hunt” against him. Mr. Trump has also said that he is aware that his conversations with foreign leaders are monitored by numerous government officials and that he would not incriminate himself so easily.</p><h2 class="css-ani50b eoo0vm40" id="link-35e91a73">What is Mr. Giuliani’s role?</h2><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Giuliani has communicated with Ukrainian officials for months about the Bidens. He has also pressed them about the circumstances of the 2016 disclosures of payments earmarked by a Russia-aligned Ukrainian political party to Paul Manafort, Mr. Trump’s 2016 campaign chairman, who is <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/03/13/us/politics/paul-manafort-sentencing.html?module=inline" title="">in federal prison</a> on convictions related to his Ukrainian political work. Mr. Giuliani has sought information about both subjects and traveled to Madrid this summer for a meeting with one of Mr. Zelensky’s top aides, whom he urged to investigate the matters.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">In May, Mr. Giuliani <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/05/09/us/politics/giuliani-ukraine-trump.html?module=inline" title="">told The New York Times</a> that he was pushing Ukraine to investigate the Bidens “because that information will be very, very helpful to my client, and may turn out to be helpful to my government.” </p><h2 class="css-ani50b eoo0vm40" id="link-7b6f5124">Did Mr. Biden do something wrong?</h2><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">No evidence has emerged that Mr. Biden was trying to help his son when he pushed for the dismissal of the Ukrainian prosecutor, who was widely seen in the West as corrupt. Stamping out high-level corruption in Ukraine had long been a central goal of Obama administration policy toward the country and a standard condition for Western aid. On Saturday, <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/21/us/politics/biden-ukraine-whistleblower-complaint.html?action=click&amp;module=inline&amp;pgtype=Homepage" title="">Mr. Biden said he had never spoken with his son</a> about any overseas work.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Biden played a lead role in the Obama administration’s diplomacy with Kiev, though administration officials worried that his son’s work for the energy<strong class="css-8qgvsz ebyp5n10"> </strong>company, Burisma Holdings, could create at least the perception of a conflict of interest. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">But Ukraine’s current top prosecutor has said <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2019-05-16/ukraine-prosecutor-says-no-evidence-of-wrongdoing-by-bidens" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">there is no evidence of wrongdoing by the Bidens</a> to investigate.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1soubk3 epkadsg3"><div class="css-15g2oxy epkadsg2"><div class="css-2b3w4o e16ij5yr6"><a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/20/us/whistleblower-law-explained.html?action=click&amp;module=RelatedLinks&amp;pgtype=Article"><div class="css-i9gxme e16ij5yr4"><div class="css-1j8dw05 e16ij5yr2">Intelligence Whistle-Blower Law, Explained</div><time class="css-x7rtpa e16638kd0" datetime="2019-09-20T18:41:56-04:00">Sept. 20, 2019</time></div><div class="css-1vm5oi9 e16ij5yr0"><img class="css-32rbo2 e16ij5yr1" src="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/20/us/politics/20dc-legal/merlin_141689673_d480a713-0bd4-429c-9b66-8c24002ba49f-threeByTwoSmallAt2X.jpg"/></div></a></div><div class="css-2b3w4o e16ij5yr6"><a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/us/politics/trump-impeachment.html?action=click&amp;module=RelatedLinks&amp;pgtype=Article"><div class="css-i9gxme e16ij5yr4"><div class="css-1j8dw05 e16ij5yr2">Highlights: Whistle-Blower Complaint Goes to House as Ukraine Phone Call Gets Released</div><time class="css-x7rtpa e16638kd0" datetime="2019-09-25T07:10:57-04:00">Sept. 25, 2019</time></div><div class="css-1vm5oi9 e16ij5yr0"><img class="css-32rbo2 e16ij5yr1" src="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/25/us/politics/25dc-impeach-briefing5/25dc-impeach-briefing5-threeByTwoSmallAt2X.jpg"/></div></a></div><div class="css-2b3w4o e16ij5yr6"><a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/05/13/us/politics/trump-investigations.html?action=click&amp;module=RelatedLinks&amp;pgtype=Article"><div class="css-i9gxme e16ij5yr4"><div class="css-1j8dw05 e16ij5yr2">Tracking 30 Investigations Related to Trump</div><time class="css-x7rtpa e16638kd0" datetime="2019-05-13T05:00:02-04:00">May 13, 2019</time></div><div class="css-1vm5oi9 e16ij5yr0"><img class="css-32rbo2 e16ij5yr1" src="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/05/10/us/trump-presidents-investigations-promo-1557500573411/trump-presidents-investigations-promo-1557500573411-threeByTwoSmallAt2X-v5.png"/></div></a></div></div></div></section><div class="bottom-of-article"><div class="css-1ubp8k9"></div><div class="css-wg1cha"><div class="css-19hdyf3 e1e7j8ap0"><div><p>Michael Crowley is a White House correspondent in the Washington bureau, where he covers President Trump’s foreign policy. He joined The Times in June 2019 from Politico, where he had been the White House and national security editor, and previously senior foreign affairs correspondent. A Washington journalism veteran, Crowley has also worked for Time magazine, The New Republic and the Boston Globe. <span class="css-4w91ra"> </span></p></div></div><div class="css-19hdyf3 e1e7j8ap0"><div><p>Ken Vogel covers the confluence of money, politics and influence from Washington.
